19                   DIRECT EXAMINATION (RESUMED)
20    BY MR. MANDIA:
21         Q.  GOOD MORNING, DR. LONGO.
22             HOW ARE YOU?
23         A.  FINE.  GOOD MORNING.
24         Q.  GOOD.
25             THIS DOCUMENT -- THIS IS WHERE WE LEFT OFF
26    YESTERDAY BEFORE WE LEFT FOR -- FOR THE DAY.
27             AND WAS THIS THE DOCUMENT THAT WE DISCUSSED
28    YESTERDAY THAT TALKED ABOUT CONCENTRATION TECHNIQUE AND
6308
 1    IT NOT BEING IN THE WORLDWIDE COMPANY INTEREST OF
 2    JOHNSON & JOHNSON TO DO THAT?
 3         A.  YES, SIR.
 4         Q.  I WANT TO TALK TO YOU NOW ABOUT SENSITIVITY OF
 5    VARIOUS METHODS USED BY THE F.D.A. AND JOHNSON &
 6    JOHNSON.
 7             AND CAN YOU FIRST EXPLAIN TO THE JURY A CONCEPT
 8    OF SENSITIVITY AS IT RELATES TO MICROSCOPY?
 9         A.  SENSITIVITY OR DETECTION LIMIT IS HOW MUCH OF
10    THE ASBESTOS FIBERS OR HOW MANY FIBERS HAS TO BE IN THE
11    SAMPLE BEFORE STATISTICALLY YOU HAVE THE ABILITY TO
12    DETECT ONE.  SO IT'S A CONCENTRATION ISSUE.
13             IF IT'S A -- TOO LOW OF A CONCENTRATION FOR THE
14    METHOD YOU ARE USING, SAY, IT'S 1,000 FIBERS PER GRAM
15    BUT -- MEANING, I HAVE TO -- IN ORDER FOR ME TO FIND
16    1 FIBER, AND MY DETECTION LIMIT IS 1,000 FIBERS PER
17    GRAM, THERE HAS TO BE 1,000 FIBERS IN THERE FOR ME TO
18    FIND ONE.
19             NOBODY HAS REACHED 1,000 FIBERS PER GRAM YET,
20    DETECTION LIMIT.
21             IF MY DETECTION LIMIT IS 10 MILLION OR
22    1 MILLION PER GRAM AND I WOULD HAVE TO FIND 1 AGAIN TO
23    GET -- THERE HAS TO BE 10 MILLION THERE TO FIND 1.
24             SAY, IT'S 15 MILLION PER GRAM.  IF I FIND 1,
25    THAT MEANS THERE IS 15 MILLION.
26             IF I FIND 0, DOESN'T MEAN THERE'S NO ASBESTOS
27    THERE; IT JUST MEANS THE METHOD THAT I USED TO PREPARE
28    THE SAMPLE WASN'T GOOD ENOUGH.  SO THAT'S SENSITIVITY.
6309
 1         Q.  AND AS I UNDERSTAND WHAT YOU ARE SAYING,
 2    DR. LONGO, YOU COULD HAVE A METHOD THAT'S NOT SENSITIVE

13    THAT THEY ARE USING FOR TRANSMISSION ELECTRON
14    MICROSCOPY, ONE, IS NOT -- DOES NOT PRODUCE A SAMPLE

16             SO THEY'RE -- WHEN THEY FIND A NEGATIVE OR
17    NON-DETECT AND SAY THERE IS NOTHING THERE, IT'S BECAUSE
18    THE SAMPLE DOESN'T HAVE TENS OF MILLIONS OF FIBERS FOR
19    THEM TO SEE 1.

21    DIFFRACTION -- AGAIN, THIS X-RAY DIFFRACTION IS A VERY
22    POOR TECHNIQUE FOR THIS TYPE OF ANALYSIS.
23             IT HAS VERY POOR ANALYTICAL SENSITIVITY, AND
24    THEY DON'T USE HEAVY LIQUID DENSITY SEPARATION TO
25    PREPARE THE SAMPLE FOR X.R.D.  PLUS YOU CAN'T TELL IF
26    IT'S FIBROUS OR NOT.
27             AND THEN THE WAY THEY REPORT THE RESULTS, IF
28    YOU SAY IT'S NON-QUANTIFIABLE AND YOU DON'T PROVIDE ANY
6326
 1    BACKUP DATA FOR THEM TO SAY NON-QUANTIFIABLE, IT MEANS
 2    THEY HAVE DETECTED ASBESTOS FIBERS OR BUNDLES, BUT THEY
 3    ARE NOT TELLING YOU HOW MANY, AND THEY ARE NOT PROVIDING
 4    YOU THE DATA.
 5             IF THERE WAS NOTHING THERE, THEY WOULD SAY IT
 6    WAS "NON-DETECT."
 7             NON-QUANTIFIABLE MEANS YES, IT'S THERE.  WE ARE
 8    NOT GOING TO TELL YOU HOW MANY.  IT'S JUST NOT ENOUGH
 9    FOR US TO SAY THAT IT'S PRESENT BECAUSE THERE MAY BE
10    SOME BACKGROUND CONTAMINATION OR SOME OTHER ISSUES.

6333
 1    WATER, AND YOU GET THIS OPTICAL ILLUSION RIGHT HERE AT
 2    THE INTERFACE?
 3             THAT'S BECAUSE THE REFRACTIVE INDICES FOR
 4    WATER, WHICH REFRACTS LIGHT, AND AIR IS DIFFERENT.  AND
 5    ALL OF YOUR REFRACTIVE INDICES WILL ALWAYS BE 1 POINT
 6    SOMETHING.
 7             SO HOW THE REFRACTIVE INDICES IS DETERMINED IS
 8    THAT YOU TAKE THE SPEED OF LIGHT GOING THROUGH A VACUUM,
 9    WHICH IS -- I ALWAYS WANT TO GET THE -- IT'S 670 MILLION
10    MILES PER HOUR.
11             AND THEN YOU TAKE THE SPEED OF LIGHT THAT IS
12    GOING THROUGH A SUBSTANCE LIKE WATER, WHICH IS A LITTLE
13    BIT SLOWER, AND YOU DIVIDE THAT.
14             AND IF YOU DIVIDE THE SPEED OF LIGHT GOING
15    THROUGH AIR, GOING THROUGH A VACUUM BY THE SPEED OF
16    LIGHT GOING THROUGH WATER, YOU WILL GET A REFRACTIVE
17    INDICES OF ABOUT POINT -- 1.2.
18             AND THE ANGLE YOU ARE LOOKING AT, BECAUSE THE
19    LIGHT IS BEING REFRACTED AT A DIFFERENT ANGLES WHEN IT
20    HITS THE PENCIL THROUGH THE WATER, MAKES IT LOOK LIKE
21    THERE IS A BREAK IN THE PENCIL.
22             NOW, WHEN YOU CHANGE THAT ANGLE -- LIKE, IF YOU
23    LOOK AT IT STRAIGHT ON, IT'S GOING TO LOOK THE SAME.
24             SO THAT'S WHAT REFRACTIVE INDICES IS.
25             AND MOST EVERYTHING WHERE LIGHT CAN TRAVEL
26    THROUGH WILL HAVE A REFRACTIVE INDICES.
27             SO WE CAN GO TO THE NEXT SLIDE.
28             NOW, EVERYBODY, I THINK, HAS PROBABLY SEEN A
6334
 1    BEAM OF LIGHT GOING THROUGH A PRISM.  AND WHEN IT GOES
 2    THROUGH A PRISM, IT IS DIVIDED INTO THE PRIMARY COLORS.
 3    AND THE REASON IS THE BEAM OF LIGHT HAS ALL THESE
 4    DIFFERENT COLORS IN IT WHICH MAKES UP THE WHITE LIGHT.
 5             IT HITS THIS ANGLE ON THE PRISM, AND THAT ANGLE
 6    WILL DISPERSE -- IT'S CALLED "DISPERSION" -- WILL
 7    DISPERSE THE DIFFERENT WAVELENGTH OF LIGHTS AT AN ANGLE
 8    AND START SEPARATING THEM.  LIKE, THE WAVELENGTH OF RED
 9    IS GOING TO BE SHORTER THAN THE WAVELENGTH FOR PURPLE.
10             SO IT'S THE DISTANCE OF THE WAVELENGTHS THAT
11    GIVES YOU THE DIFFERENT COLORS; SO IT IS DISPERSED HERE.
12    AND AS IT LEAVES THE PRISM, IT'S ANOTHER ANGLE, AND IT'S
13    DISPERSED WIDER.
14             THAT DISPERSION IS USED BY POLARIZED LIGHT
15    MICROSCOPY TO DETERMINE WHAT WAVELENGTH OF LIGHT IS
16    DISPERSED.  DISPERSION OUT OF THE CRYSTAL.
17             AND BY MEASURING THE WAVELENGTHS OF LIGHT YOU
18    CAN GET THE REFRACTIVE INDICES BECAUSE YOU -- AND THEN
19    FROM THERE, YOU CAN IDENTIFY THE CRYSTAL.
20             IT TOOK ME MONTHS AND MONTHS AND MONTHS TO
21    UNDERSTAND THE WHOLE PROCESS.  SO I APOLOGIZE.  BUT IT
22    GIVES YOU THIS COLOR AND WE -- AND THE DISPERSION IS
23    USED TO IDENTIFY CRYSTALS LIKE ASBESTOS AND FIBROUS
24    TALC.

6352
 1             HOWEVER, THE ONE DIFFERENCE IS WE ARE NOT USING
 2    THE SAME REFRACTIVE INDICES FLUID.
 3             CHRYSOTILE AND FIBROUS TALC IS BEST IDENTIFIED
 4    USING A FLUID OF 1.550.  ON THE OTHER HAND, THE
 5    AMPHIBOLE ASBESTOS FOUND IN COSMETIC TALCS IS BEST
 6    IDENTIFIED BY 1.605 REFRACTIVE INDICES FLUID.
 7             BECAUSE YOU HAVE DIFFERENT REFRACTIVE INDICES
 8    THAT ARE CLOSER TO THE 1.605 THAN IT IS FOR THE 1.550.
 9             WHAT YOU ARE TRYING TO DO IS GET A REFRACTIVE
10    INDICES FLUID THAT IS CLOSE TO THE REFRACTIVE INDICES
11    FLUIDS THAT -- THE REFRACTIVE INDICES OF THE ASBESTOS
12    YOU ARE LOOKING AT.
13             IT MAKES IT A LOT EASIER.  AND IF YOU DON'T GET
14    THE RIGHT REFRACTIVE INDICES FLUID, YOUR REFRACTIVE
15    INDICES WOULD BE WAY OUT OF RANGE, AND IT WOULDN'T MAKE
16    ANY SENSE TO YOU.  SO IT'S IMPORTANT TO USE THE RIGHT
17    FLUID.  THAT'S THE ONLY DIFFERENCE.  ALL THE SCIENCE IS
18    THE SAME.

22    MINE SOURCES.

24    DETERMINED THERE'S ASBESTOS?

 1    BY MR. MANDIA:
 2         Q.  THERE WERE SOME QUESTIONS OF YOU ABOUT ASBESTOS
 3    AND NON-ASBESTOS.  FROM WHAT YOU FOUND IN THE JOHNSON'S
 4    BABY POWDER, AS IT PERTAINS TO TREMOLITE, DID YOU FIND
 5    ASBESTOS OR NON-ASBESTOS?
 6         A.  WE FOUND BOTH.  WE DIDN'T COUNT THE
 7    NON-ASBESTOS CLEAVAGE FRAGMENTS.  WE HAVE DOCUMENTED
 8    THAT THEY ARE IN THERE, BUT WE HAVE ONLY REGULATED
 9    TREMOLITE ASBESTOS.

11    ASBESTOS ACTINOLITE OR NON-ASBESTOS ACTINOLITE?
12         A.  WE FOUND BOTH.  WE ONLY REPORTED THE
13    ASBESTOS -- WE CALL IT TREMOLITE-ACTINOLITE.
14         Q.  AS IT PERTAINS TO ANTHOPHYLLITE, DID YOU FIND
15    THE NON-ASBESTOS ANTHOPHYLLITE OR THE ASBESTOS
16    ANTHOPHYLLITE?

18    HAD FOUND THE NON-ASBESTOS CLEAVAGE FRAGMENT TREMOLITE
19    AS WELL AS TREMOLITE ASBESTOS.  AND SOME OF THE SAMPLES
20    WERE ONLY THE CLEAVAGE FRAGMENTS, FROM THE SAME MINE.
21             SO YOU'LL HAVE BOTH.  IF YOU FIND ONE, YOU'LL
22    ALWAYS FIND THE OTHER.
23         Q.  AND AS IT PERTAINS TO CHRYSOTILE, IS THAT BY
24    ITS NATURE AND FORM CONSIDERED ASBESTOS?

26    PRONOUNCE IT CHRYSOTILE THAT IT IS, IN FACT, ASBESTOS.
27    YOU DON'T GET THIS ARGUMENT OF CLEAVAGE FRAGMENTS OF
28    CHRYSOTILE LIKE YOU DO WITH THE AMPHIBOLES.
6507
 1         Q.  AND IF IT'S A BUNDLE -- AND YOU HAVE TOLD THE
 2    JURY ABOUT DETECTING BUNDLES -- WOULD THAT BE ASBESTOS
 3    OR NON-ASBESTOS?
 4         A.  THERE'S AN AGREEMENT IN THE SCIENTIFIC
 5    COMMUNITY THAT IF IT IS A BUNDLE, BY -- BECAUSE IT IS A
 6    BUNDLE, IT IS ASBESTOS.  IF IT HAS ALL THE -- HAS THE
 7    CHEMISTRY AND THE DIFFRACTION PATTERN.
 8             BECAUSE THINK ABOUT WHAT WE HAVE BEEN TALKING
 9    ABOUT.  SMASHING A ROCK.  HOW DO YOU GET ALL THOSE NICE
10    FIBERS TO LINE UP TOGETHER, ALL -- ALL PUSHED INTO ONE
11    GEOMETRICAL SHAPE IF IT'S FROM CRUSHING A ROCK.  IT
12    DOESN'T MAKE ANY SENSE.
13             AND THAT'S WHY, IF IT'S A BUNDLE MOST -- MOST
14    OF THE EXPERTS WILL SAY "WELL, THAT'S ASBESTIFORM.  JUST
15    THE FACT THAT IT'S A BUNDLE."

11         Q.  AND EXPLAIN TO THE JURY, TO THE EXTENT THEY
12    HAVEN'T ALREADY HEARD IT, WHAT THE PEER-REVIEW PROCESS
13    IS.
14         A.  THERE IS HUNDREDS OF JOURNALS -- SCIENTIFIC
15    JOURNALS -- OUT IN THE REAL WORLD, I GUESS, AND THEY GO
16    AND COVER ALL KINDS OF TOPICS.
17             THE TOPICS THAT I AM TYPICALLY TEST- -- PUTTING
18    PAPERS IN IS THINGS THAT DO WITH SOME TYPE OF EXPOSURE
19    TO ASBESTOS.
20             LIKE THE -- THE JOURNAL OF CANCER.  BUT A LOT
21    OF THE PAPERS GO INTO THINGS LIKE OCCUPATIONAL AND
22    SAFETY AND HEALTH-TYPE.
23             AND SO ONCE YOU PICK A JOURNAL, THEN YOU WRITE,
24    AND IT HAS TO BE SOMETHING NEW -- NEW RESEARCH.  AND YOU
25    WRITE IT UP ON HOW YOU DID IT, CONCLUSIONS, ET CETERA,
26    AND THEN YOU SEND IT TO A JOURNAL.
27             THE FIRST PERSON WHO IS GOING TO READ THAT IS
28    THE EDITOR OF THE JOURNAL.  HE WILL MAKE A DECISION
6514
 1    "YES, THIS BELONGS IN OUR JOURNAL."
 2             OR, B, "NO, THIS IS NOT THE TYPE OF SCIENCE OR
 3    RESEARCH WE ARE LOOKING FOR.  AND WE'LL SEND IT BACK
 4    WITH A LETTER SAYING 'WE DON'T TAKE THESE TYPES OF
 5    STUDIES.'"
 6             ONCE HE DECIDES THAT THEY ARE GOING TO THINK
 7    ABOUT PUBLISHING, THEY'LL SEND IT OUT TO YOUR PEERS.
 8    AND THESE WILL BE OTHER SCIENTISTS IN YOUR FIELD WHO
 9    WILL EVALUATE YOUR -- YOUR STUDIES.
10             AND IT'S SUPPOSED TO BE ALL CONFIDENTIAL, THAT
11    YOU DON'T -- THEY DON'T KNOW WHO PUT -- PUT THE PAPER
12    IN, AND YOU DON'T KNOW WHO IS EVALUATING YOUR PAPER.
13             SO THAT IF YOU RUN INTO THEM AGAIN AT THE NEXT
14    CONFERENCE, YOU ARE NOT MAD AT THEM.
15             AND ONCE THEY SAY "OKAY," THEY CAN DO A COUPLE
16    OF THINGS WITH THIS.
17             THEY CAN SAY "NO, THIS IS NOT NEW SCIENCE.
18    IT'S -- IT DOESN'T MEET THE STANDARD."  AND WE REJECT
19    IT.
20             OR THEY MAY ASK SOME QUESTIONS FOR YOU TO
21    ADDRESS.  AND THEY'LL GO ALL THE WAY TO THE "YOU NEED TO
22    AT LEAST PUT IT INTO REALLY ACCEPTABLE GRAMMAR FOR THIS
23    JOURNAL" AND ACCEPT IT.
24             AND THAT'S THE WHOLE PEER-REVIEW PROCESS.
